# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes API Server Admission Controller Chain

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the API server admission controller pipeline: the admission.Interface registration, the generic admission chain execution, the mutating admission ordering, and the validating admission webhook call.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I have successfully analyzed the Kubernetes API server admission controller pipeline and created a comprehensive answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

I've identified and documented **22 core Go source files** implementing the API server admission controller pipeline in kubernetes/kubernetes, along with **30+ key symbols** and the **11-function execution chain**.

### Key Components Found:

**Core Interfaces & Chain:**
- `admission.Interface` - base abstraction
- `admission.MutationInterface` - for mutating phase
- `admission.ValidationInterface` - for validating phase
- `chainAdmissionHandler` - sequential execution of handlers

**Execution Pipeline:**
1. `AdmissionOptions.ApplyTo()` - configuration entry point
2. `Plugins.NewFromPlugins()` - builds the chain
3. `chainAdmissionHandler.Admit()` - runs mutating phase
4. `reinvoker` wrapper - handles re-invocation policies
5. `chainAdmissionHandler.Validate()` - runs validating phase
6. Decorators like `WithAudit()` and `WithStepMetrics()` wrap the chain

**Webhook Integration:**
- Mutating webhooks via `mutatingDispatcher`
- Validating webhooks via `validatingDispatcher`
- Configuration managers for dynamic webhook management

**Plugin Registration:**
- Generic plugins in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/plugins.go`
- Kube-apiserver specific plugins in `pkg/kubeapiserver/options/plugins.go`

The narrative explanation in the answer file provides a comprehensive walkthrough of how requests flow through the admission controller pipeline from initial interface definitions through to request handling.

This is a different resource, scoped to the parent resource, but it may have a different kind.\n41: \t// For instance, /pods has the resource \"pods\" and the kind \"Pod\", while /pods/foo/status has the resource \"pods\", the sub resource \"status\", and the kind \"Pod\"\n42: \t// (because status operates on pods). implemented across multiple files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository, centered around the admission.Interface abstraction and its two main implementations: MutationInterface for mutating webhooks and ValidationInterface for validating webhooks.\\n\\nCore Interface Definitions (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go):\\nThe admission system is built on the admission.Interface, which defines the Handles(operation) method to determine if a handler can process a request. MutationInterface extends Interface with Admit(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for mutating admissions, and ValidationInterface provides Validate(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for validation-only admissions. The Attributes and ObjectInterfaces interfaces provide request context and object handling capabilities.\\n\\nAdmission Chain Execution (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go):\\nThe chainAdmissionHandler is a []Interface slice that implements the admission chain pattern. It executes handlers sequentially: the Admit() method iterates through handlers calling Admit() on MutationInterface types, and Validate() iterates through handlers calling Validate() on ValidationInterface types. Both return immediately on first error.\\n\\nReinvocation Support (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/reinvocation.go):\\nThe newReinvocationHandler() function wraps the admission chain in a reinvoker struct that implements reinvocation policies. The reinvoker's Admit() method checks if re-invocation is needed after the initial admission phase and reinvokes the chain if required. This allows mutating webhooks to be re-run if earlier mutations require validation of modified objects.\\n\\nPlugin Management and Chain Building (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go):\\nThe Plugins type manages plugin registration and instantiation. The NewFromPlugins() method builds the complete admission chain by: (1) iterating through plugin names, (2) instantiating each plugin, (3) separating plugins into mutation and validation lists, (4) wrapping handlers with optional decorators, and (5) wrapping the final chain with newReinvocationHandler(). This method returns the wrapped chain.\\n\\nPlugin Registration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/plugins.go and pkg/kubeapiserver/options/plugins.go):\\nRegisterAllAdmissionPlugins() registers both generic plugins (lifecycle, mutating/validating webhooks, policies) and kube-apiserver specific plugins. The registration order is irrelevant at registration time but execution order is strictly controlled: all mutating plugins run before validating plugins.\\n\\nAdmission Options and Configuration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/admission.go):\\nAdmissionOptions holds plugin names, configuration file path, and decorators. The ApplyTo() method is responsible for: (1) reading plugin configuration, (2) creating plugin initializers, (3) building the admission chain via Plugins.NewFromPlugins(), (4) wrapping with metrics via WithStepMetrics(), and (5) storing in server config as AdmissionControl.\\n\\nMutating Admission Webhooks (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go):\\nThe mutating Plugin implements admission.MutationInterface. Register() adds it to the plugins registry. NewMutatingWebhook() instantiates it with a handler and dispatcher. The Admit() method delegates to the generic Webhook's Dispatch() which invokes configured MutatingWebhookConfiguration objects in deterministic order via mutatingDispatcher.\\n\\nValidating Admission Webhooks (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go):\\nThe validating Plugin implements admission.ValidationInterface with similar structure to mutating webhooks. NewValidatingAdmissionWebhook() creates it with a dispatcher. The Validate() method delegates to generic Webhook's Dispatch() which invokes ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects via validatingDispatcher.\\n\\nWebhook Dispatchers (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go and validating/dispatcher.go):\\nmutatingDispatcher and validatingDispatcher implement the generic.Dispatcher interface. They manage webhook execution, including handling re-invocation contexts, applying patches (for mutating), and enforcing failure policies. They work with WebhookAccessors obtained from configuration managers.\\n\\nWebhook Configuration Managers (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/):\\nmutatingWebhookConfigurationManager and validatingWebhookConfigurationManager manage dynamic webhook configurations. They list and cache MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects respectively, ensuring deterministic ordering and efficient recompilation of webhook policies.\\n\\nDecorators and Wrappers:\\nThe decorator.Decorator interface allows wrapping handlers with additional behavior. WithAudit() (audit.go) wraps handlers to log admission annotations to audit events. WithStepMetrics() (metrics/metrics.go) instruments admission with prometheus metrics. These are applied via the Decorators slice in NewFromPlugins().\\n\\nRequest Handling Integration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/):\\nIn create.go, update.go, delete.go, and rest.go, handlers check if admit is a MutationInterface and call Admit(), then check if it's ValidationInterface and call Validate(). The admission chain is invoked after authorization but before persistence, with attributes like operation type (CREATE, UPDATE, DELETE, CONNECT), request object, old object (for updates), and user info.\\n\\nExecution Flow Summary:\\n1. Client request arrives at API server\\n2. Authentication and authorization complete\\n3. Request body deserialized\\n4. AdmissionControl interface (the wrapped chain) is invoked\\n5. Mutating phase: chainAdmissionHandler.Admit() runs all mutating plugins/webhooks in order\\n6. Reinvocation check: if mutations occurred, reinvoker may reinvoke the chain\\n7. Validating phase: chainAdmissionHandler.Validate() runs all validating plugins/webhooks\\n8. If any handler rejects, request fails; otherwise proceeds to persistence\\n\\nThe admission system achieves its goals through this layered architecture: the Interface abstraction allows pluggability, chainAdmissionHandler provides sequential execution, reinvoker handles re-invocation policies, decorators add cross-cutting concerns (audit, metrics), and webhook dispatchers manage dynamic configuration of MutatingAdmissionWebhook and ValidatingAdmissionWebhook resources.\"\n}\n",

implemented across multiple files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository, centered around the admission.Interface abstraction and its two main implementations: MutationInterface for mutating webhooks and ValidationInterface for validating webhooks.\\n\\nCore Interface Definitions (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go):\\nThe admission system is built on the admission.Interface, which defines the Handles(operation) method to determine if a handler can process a request. MutationInterface extends Interface with Admit(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for mutating admissions, and ValidationInterface provides Validate(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for validation-only admissions. The Attributes and ObjectInterfaces interfaces provide request context and object handling capabilities.\\n\\nAdmission Chain Execution (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go):\\nThe chainAdmissionHandler is a []Interface slice that implements the admission chain pattern. It executes handlers sequentially: the Admit() method iterates through handlers calling Admit() on MutationInterface types, and Validate() iterates through handlers calling Validate() on ValidationInterface types. Both return immediately on first error.\\n\\nReinvocation Support (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/reinvocation.go):\\nThe newReinvocationHandler() function wraps the admission chain in a reinvoker struct that implements reinvocation policies. The reinvoker's Admit() method checks if re-invocation is needed after the initial admission phase and reinvokes the chain if required. This allows mutating webhooks to be re-run if earlier mutations require validation of modified objects.\\n\\nPlugin Management and Chain Building (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go):\\nThe Plugins type manages plugin registration and instantiation. The NewFromPlugins() method builds the complete admission chain by: (1) iterating through plugin names, (2) instantiating each plugin, (3) separating plugins into mutation and validation lists, (4) wrapping handlers with optional decorators, and (5) wrapping the final chain with newReinvocationHandler(). This method returns the wrapped chain.\\n\\nPlugin Registration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/plugins.go and pkg/kubeapiserver/options/plugins.go):\\nRegisterAllAdmissionPlugins() registers both generic plugins (lifecycle, mutating/validating webhooks, policies) and kube-apiserver specific plugins. The registration order is irrelevant at registration time but execution order is strictly controlled: all mutating plugins run before validating plugins.\\n\\nAdmission Options and Configuration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/admission.go):\\nAdmissionOptions holds plugin names, configuration file path, and decorators. The ApplyTo() method is responsible for: (1) reading plugin configuration, (2) creating plugin initializers, (3) building the admission chain via Plugins.NewFromPlugins(), (4) wrapping with metrics via WithStepMetrics(), and (5) storing in server config as AdmissionControl.\\n\\nMutating Admission Webhooks (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go):\\nThe mutating Plugin implements admission.MutationInterface. Register() adds it to the plugins registry. NewMutatingWebhook() instantiates it with a handler and dispatcher. The Admit() method delegates to the generic Webhook's Dispatch() which invokes configured MutatingWebhookConfiguration objects in deterministic order via mutatingDispatcher.\\n\\nValidating Admission Webhooks (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go):\\nThe validating Plugin implements admission.ValidationInterface with similar structure to mutating webhooks. NewValidatingAdmissionWebhook() creates it with a dispatcher. The Validate() method delegates to generic Webhook's Dispatch() which invokes ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects via validatingDispatcher.\\n\\nWebhook Dispatchers (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go and validating/dispatcher.go):\\nmutatingDispatcher and validatingDispatcher implement the generic.Dispatcher interface. They manage webhook execution, including handling re-invocation contexts, applying patches (for mutating), and enforcing failure policies. They work with WebhookAccessors obtained from configuration managers.\\n\\nWebhook Configuration Managers (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/):\\nmutatingWebhookConfigurationManager and validatingWebhookConfigurationManager manage dynamic webhook configurations. They list and cache MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects respectively, ensuring deterministic ordering and efficient recompilation of webhook policies.\\n\\nDecorators and Wrappers:\\nThe decorator.Decorator interface allows wrapping handlers with additional behavior. WithAudit() (audit.go) wraps handlers to log admission annotations to audit events. WithStepMetrics() (metrics/metrics.go) instruments admission with prometheus metrics. These are applied via the Decorators slice in NewFromPlugins().\\n\\nRequest Handling Integration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/):\\nIn create.go, update.go, delete.go, and rest.go, handlers check if admit is a MutationInterface and call Admit(), then check if it's ValidationInterface and call Validate(). The admission chain is invoked after authorization but before persistence, with attributes like operation type (CREATE, UPDATE, DELETE, CONNECT), request object, old object (for updates), and user info.\\n\\nExecution Flow Summary:\\n1. Client request arrives at API server\\n2. Authentication and authorization complete\\n3. Request body deserialized\\n4. AdmissionControl interface (the wrapped chain) is invoked\\n5. Mutating phase: chainAdmissionHandler.Admit() runs all mutating plugins/webhooks in order\\n6. Reinvocation check: if mutations occurred, reinvoker may reinvoke the chain\\n7. Validating phase: chainAdmissionHandler.Validate() runs all validating plugins/webhooks\\n8. If any handler rejects, request fails; otherwise proceeds to persistence\\n\\nThe admission system achieves its goals through this layered architecture: the Interface abstraction allows pluggability, chainAdmissionHandler provides sequential execution, reinvoker handles re-invocation policies, decorators add cross-cutting concerns (audit, metrics), and webhook dispatchers manage dynamic configuration of MutatingAdmissionWebhook and ValidatingAdmissionWebhook resources.\"\n}\n",

This method returns the wrapped chain.\\n\\nPlugin Registration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/plugins.go and pkg/kubeapiserver/options/plugins.go):\\nRegisterAllAdmissionPlugins() registers both generic plugins (lifecycle, mutating/validating webhooks, policies) and kube-apiserver specific plugins. The registration order is irrelevant at registration time but execution order is strictly controlled: all mutating plugins run before validating plugins.\\n\\nAdmission Options and Configuration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/admission.go):\\nAdmissionOptions holds plugin names, configuration file path, and decorators. The ApplyTo() method is responsible for: (1) reading plugin configuration, (2) creating plugin initializers, (3) building the admission chain via Plugins.NewFromPlugins(), (4) wrapping with metrics via WithStepMetrics(), and (5) storing in server config as AdmissionControl.\\n\\nMutating Admission Webhooks (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go):\\nThe mutating Plugin implements admission.MutationInterface. Register() adds it to the plugins registry. NewMutatingWebhook() instantiates it with a handler and dispatcher. The Admit() method delegates to the generic Webhook's Dispatch() which invokes configured MutatingWebhookConfiguration objects in deterministic order via mutatingDispatcher.\\n\\nValidating Admission Webhooks (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go):\\nThe validating Plugin implements admission.ValidationInterface with similar structure to mutating webhooks. NewValidatingAdmissionWebhook() creates it with a dispatcher. The Validate() method delegates to generic Webhook's Dispatch() which invokes ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects via validatingDispatcher.\\n\\nWebhook Dispatchers (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go and validating/dispatcher.go):\\nmutatingDispatcher and validatingDispatcher implement the generic.Dispatcher interface. They manage webhook execution, including handling re-invocation contexts, applying patches (for mutating), and enforcing failure policies. They work with WebhookAccessors obtained from configuration managers.\\n\\nWebhook Configuration Managers (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/):\\nmutatingWebhookConfigurationManager and validatingWebhookConfigurationManager manage dynamic webhook configurations. They list and cache MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects respectively, ensuring deterministic ordering and efficient recompilation of webhook policies.\\n\\nDecorators and Wrappers:\\nThe decorator.Decorator interface allows wrapping handlers with additional behavior. WithAudit() (audit.go) wraps handlers to log admission annotations to audit events. WithStepMetrics() (metrics/metrics.go) instruments admission with prometheus metrics. These are applied via the Decorators slice in NewFromPlugins().\\n\\nRequest Handling Integration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/):\\nIn create.go, update.go, delete.go, and rest.go, handlers check if admit is a MutationInterface and call Admit(), then check if it's ValidationInterface and call Validate(). The admission chain is invoked after authorization but before persistence, with attributes like operation type (CREATE, UPDATE, DELETE, CONNECT), request object, old object (for updates), and user info.\\n\\nExecution Flow Summary:\\n1. Client request arrives at API server\\n2. Authentication and authorization complete\\n3. Request body deserialized\\n4. AdmissionControl interface (the wrapped chain) is invoked\\n5. Mutating phase: chainAdmissionHandler.Admit() runs all mutating plugins/webhooks in order\\n6. Reinvocation check: if mutations occurred, reinvoker may reinvoke the chain\\n7. Validating phase: chainAdmissionHandler.Validate() runs all validating plugins/webhooks\\n8. If any handler rejects, request fails; otherwise proceeds to persistence\\n\\nThe admission system achieves its goals through this layered architecture: the Interface abstraction allows pluggability, chainAdmissionHandler provides sequential execution, reinvoker handles re-invocation policies, decorators add cross-cutting concerns (audit, metrics), and webhook dispatchers manage dynamic configuration of MutatingAdmissionWebhook and ValidatingAdmissionWebhook resources.\"\n}\n",
